## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law relates the reaction rate to the concentration of reactants, potentially with various order dependencies.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Reaction rate independent of concentration, constant rate'}
- {'name': 'First-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)'}
- {'name': 'Second-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to square of concentration (bimolecular reaction)'}
- {'name': 'nth-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'General power-law rate dependence on concentration'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order / saturation kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)', 'scenario': 'Rate saturates at high concentration (enzyme-like or catalytic surface reaction)'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order forward and reverse reaction approaching equilibrium'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Product catalyzes its own formation, logistic-type rate'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive/parallel reaction with time dependence', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t)', 'scenario': 'First-order decay with contribution from intermediate species'}
- {'name': 'Second-order with equilibrium offset', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2', 'scenario': 'Polynomial rate law capturing multiple reaction pathways'}
- {'name': 'Inhibition kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2)', 'scenario': 'Substrate inhibition at high concentrations'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent rate coefficient', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A', 'scenario': 'Reaction with time-varying conditions (e.g., temperature ramp)'}
- {'name': 'Fractional order with offset', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2', 'scenario': 'General fractional order kinetics with background rate'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative dA/dt with positive A suggests consumption/decay kinetics → rate = -k * A^n with k > 0
- Rate approaching zero as A approaches zero → power-law dependence dA_dt ~ A^n with n > 0
- Rate leveling off at high concentration → saturation form A/(c + A) or A/(c + A^2)
- Rate changing sign at specific A values → equilibrium/reversible reaction with terms like c0*A + c1
- Quadratic dependence on A with a maximum rate at intermediate concentration → autocatalytic form A*(c - A)
- If dA/dt depends on t explicitly beyond through A(t) → hidden intermediate species or non-isothermal conditions
- Log-linear relationship between rate and concentration → first-order or nth-order kinetics (log(rate) = n*log(A) + const)
- Rate proportional to product of concentration differences → parallel or competitive reaction pathways

1. A quadratic term in A: `-c₀*A²`

- **sin(√A)** - a sine of square root of A
- **A*exp(linear in t)** - product of A with exponential in t
- **A²** - quadratic in A

Could any candidate's free constants be set to produce sin(√A)? No - none of the candidates have a sine function with √A or any function of A inside a sine.
